<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Ellen Burstyn</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>

<p><b>Ellen Burstyn</b> (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/N%C3%A9e" title="Née">née</a></i> <b>Edna Rae Gillooly</b>; December 7, 1932) is an American actress. Her career began in theatre during the late 1950s, and over the next decade included several films and television series.</p>
<p>Burstyn's performance in the acclaimed 1971 ensemble drama <i><a href="/wiki/The_Last_Picture_Show" title="The Last Picture Show">The Last Picture Show</a></i> brought her first <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actress" title="Academy Award for Best Supporting Actress">Academy Award for Best Supporting Actress</a> nomination, after which she moved from supporting to leading film and stage roles. Burstyn received a second Academy Award nomination for her lead performance in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Exorcist_(film)" title="The Exorcist (film)">The Exorcist</a></i> (1973), and won the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Actress" title="Academy Award for Best Actress">Academy Award for Best Actress</a> the following year for her work in <a href="/wiki/Martin_Scorsese" title="Martin Scorsese">Martin Scorsese</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Alice_Doesn%27t_Live_Here_Anymore" title="Alice Doesn't Live Here Anymore">Alice Doesn't Live Here Anymore</a></i>.</p>
<p>In 1975, she won the <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award" title="Tony Award">Tony Award</a> for her lead performance in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Broadway_(theatre)" title="Broadway (theatre)">Broadway</a> production of <i><a href="/wiki/Same_Time,_Next_Year_(play)" title="Same Time, Next Year (play)">Same Time, Next Year</a></i>, and received a <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award" title="Golden Globe Award">Golden Globe Award</a> and a fourth Academy Award nomination for her performance in the 1978 <a href="/wiki/Same_Time,_Next_Year_(film)" title="Same Time, Next Year (film)">film version</a> of the play.</p>
<p>Burstyn has worked consistently in film, television and theatre since, receiving multiple awards and nominations along the way, including seven additional <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award" title="Golden Globe Award">Golden Globe Award</a> nominations, five <a href="/wiki/Emmy_Award" title="Emmy Award">Emmy Award</a> nominations (two wins), and two more <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Actress" title="Academy Award for Best Actress">Academy Award for Best Actress</a> nominations for her performances in the films <i><a href="/wiki/Resurrection_(1980_film)" title="Resurrection (1980 film)">Resurrection</a></i> (1980) and <i><a href="/wiki/Requiem_for_a_Dream" title="Requiem for a Dream">Requiem for a Dream</a></i> (2000).</p>
<p>Burstyn is one of the very few performers to have won the <a href="/wiki/Triple_Crown_of_Acting" title="Triple Crown of Acting">Triple Crown of Acting</a>. In 2013, she was inducted into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_Theatre_Hall_of_Fame" title="American Theatre Hall of Fame">American Theatre Hall of Fame</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ellen_Burstyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Burstyn was born <b>Edna Rae Gillooly</b> in <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">Michigan</a>, the daughter of Correine Marie (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Married_and_maiden_names" title="Married and maiden names">née</a> Hamel) and John Austin Gillooly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lessons_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-lessons-2">[2]</a></sup> She has described her ancestry as "Irish, French, <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Dutch" title="Pennsylvania Dutch">Pennsylvania Dutch</a>, a little <a href="/wiki/Aboriginal_peoples_in_Canada" title="Aboriginal peoples in Canada">Canadian Indian</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-clark_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-clark-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-time_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-time-4">[4]</a></sup> Burstyn has an older brother, Jack, and a younger brother, Steve.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lessons_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-lessons-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Her parents divorced when she was young and she and her brothers lived with her mother and her stepfather.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lessons_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-lessons-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>She attended <a href="/wiki/Cass_Technical_High_School" title="Cass Technical High School">Cass Technical High School</a>, a <a href="/wiki/University-preparatory_school" title="University-preparatory school">university-preparatory school</a> which allowed students to choose a specific field of study. Burstyn majored in fashion illustration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> In high school, she was a cheerleader, a member of the student council and was president of her junior class. She dropped out of high school during her senior year after failing her classes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sweeney_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-sweeney-8">[8]</a></sup> After dropping out of school, Burstyn got a job as a model in a Detroit department store. She later relocated to <a href="/wiki/Dallas" title="Dallas">Dallas</a> where she continued modeling before traveling to <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>.</p>
<p>From 1955 to 1956, Burstyn appeared as an "away we go" dancing girl on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Jackie_Gleason_Show" title="The Jackie Gleason Show">The Jackie Gleason Show</a></i> under the name "Erica Dean."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bio_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-bio-9">[9]</a></sup> Burstyn then decided to become an actress and chose the name "Ellen McRae" as her professional name; she would later change her surname after her 1964 marriage to Neil Burstyn.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-glover_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-glover-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ellen_Burstyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years">Early years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ellen_Burstyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Burstyn debuted on <a href="/wiki/Broadway_theatre" title="Broadway theatre">Broadway</a> in 1957 and joined <a href="/wiki/Lee_Strasberg" title="Lee Strasberg">Lee Strasberg</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Actors_Studio" title="Actors Studio">The Actors Studio</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, New York, in 1967. In 1975, she won a <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award" title="Tony Award">Tony Award</a> for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tony_Award_for_Best_Performance_by_a_Leading_Actress_in_a_Play" title="Tony Award for Best Performance by a Leading Actress in a Play">Best Performance by a Leading Actress in a Play</a> for her performance in the comedy <i><a href="/wiki/Same_Time,_Next_Year_(play)" title="Same Time, Next Year (play)">Same Time, Next Year</a></i> (a role she would reprise in the <a href="/wiki/Same_Time,_Next_Year_(film)" title="Same Time, Next Year (film)">film version in 1978</a>).</p>
<p>Starting in the late 1950s and continuing throughout the 1960s, Burstyn frequently played guest roles on a number of <a href="/wiki/Prime_time" title="Prime time">primetime</a> television shows, including <i><a href="/wiki/Dr._Kildare_(TV_series)" title="Dr. Kildare (TV series)">Dr. Kildare</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/77_Sunset_Strip" title="77 Sunset Strip">77 Sunset Strip</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Ben_Casey" title="Ben Casey">Ben Casey</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Gunsmoke" title="Gunsmoke">Gunsmoke</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Perry_Mason_(TV_series)" title="Perry Mason (TV series)">Perry Mason</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Wagon_Train" title="Wagon Train">Wagon Train</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Big_Valley" title="The Big Valley">The Big Valley</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Virginian_(TV_series)" title="The Virginian (TV series)">The Virginian</a></i>. During 1964-1965, she had a recurring role as "Dr. Kate Bartok" on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Broadcasting_Company" title="National Broadcasting Company">NBC</a> <a href="/wiki/Daytime_television" title="Daytime television">daytime television</a> <a href="/wiki/Soap_opera" title="Soap opera">soap opera</a> <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Doctors_(soap_opera)" title="The Doctors (soap opera)">The Doctors</a></i>. In 1967-1968, she co-starred as "Julie Parsons" opposite <a href="/wiki/Dale_Robertson" title="Dale Robertson">Dale Robertson</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company_(ABC)" title="American Broadcasting Company (ABC)">ABC</a> <a href="/wiki/Westerns_on_television" title="Westerns on television">western</a> <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Iron_Horse_(TV_series)" title="The Iron Horse (TV series)">The Iron Horse</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> She was credited as "Ellen McRae" until 1967, when she and her then-husband Neil Nephew both changed their surname to "Burstyn" and she began to be credited as "Ellen Burstyn".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1970s.E2.80.931980s">1970s–1980s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ellen_Burstyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1970s–1980s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1971, Burstyn received <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a> nominations for <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actress" title="Academy Award for Best Supporting Actress">Best Supporting Actress</a> for her role in the drama film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Last_Picture_Show" title="The Last Picture Show">The Last Picture Show</a></i> and for <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Actress" title="Academy Award for Best Actress">Best Actress</a> in 1973 for the horror film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Exorcist_(film)" title="The Exorcist (film)">The Exorcist</a></i>. During the filming of <i>The Exorcist</i>, she injured her <a href="/wiki/Coccyx" title="Coccyx">coccyx</a>, which led to permanent injury to her spine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> She won the Academy Award for Best Actress in 1974 for her performance in the drama <i><a href="/wiki/Alice_Doesn%27t_Live_Here_Anymore" title="Alice Doesn't Live Here Anymore">Alice Doesn't Live Here Anymore</a></i>, directed by <a href="/wiki/Martin_Scorsese" title="Martin Scorsese">Martin Scorsese</a>. She also received Best Actress nominations in 1978 for <i>Same Time, Next Year</i>, in 1980 for the drama <i><a href="/wiki/Resurrection_(1980_film)" title="Resurrection (1980 film)">Resurrection</a></i>, and for the drama <i><a href="/wiki/Requiem_for_a_Dream" title="Requiem for a Dream">Requiem for a Dream</a></i> in 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT2_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT2-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EllenBurstyn07TIFF.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="807" data-file-width="647" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/EllenBurstyn07TIFF.jpg/170px-EllenBurstyn07TIFF.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/EllenBurstyn07TIFF.jpg/255px-EllenBurstyn07TIFF.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/EllenBurstyn07TIFF.jpg/340px-EllenBurstyn07TIFF.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EllenBurstyn07TIFF.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Burstyn at the <a href="/wiki/2007_Toronto_International_Film_Festival" title="2007 Toronto International Film Festival">2007 Toronto International Film Festival</a>, September 2007</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1977, she was a member of the jury at the <a href="/wiki/27th_Berlin_International_Film_Festival" title="27th Berlin International Film Festival">27th Berlin International Film Festival</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Berlinale_1977_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Berlinale_1977-15">[15]</a></sup> and in 1988, she was a member of the jury for the <a href="/wiki/38th_Berlin_International_Film_Festival" title="38th Berlin International Film Festival">38th Berlin International Film Festival</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Berlinale_1988_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Berlinale_1988-16">[16]</a></sup> Burstyn hosted NBC's <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">Saturday Night Live</a></i>, a late-night <a href="/wiki/Sketch_comedy" title="Sketch comedy">sketch comedy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Variety_show" title="Variety show">variety show</a>, in December 1980.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-preston_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-preston-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1986, Burstyn starred in her own <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a> television <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Situation_comedy" title="Situation comedy">situation comedy</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ellen_Burstyn_Show" title="The Ellen Burstyn Show">The Ellen Burstyn Show</a></i> costarring <a href="/wiki/Megan_Mullally" title="Megan Mullally">Megan Mullally</a> as her daughter and <a href="/wiki/Elaine_Stritch" title="Elaine Stritch">Elaine Stritch</a> as her mother; it was canceled after one season.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1990s.E2.80.93present">1990s–present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ellen_Burstyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1990s–present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1990, she won the <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Siddons_Award" title="Sarah Siddons Award">Sarah Siddons Award</a> for her work in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Theatre_in_Chicago" title="Theatre in Chicago">Chicago theatre</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-siddons_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-siddons-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>From 2000 to 2002, Burstyn appeared in the <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a> television drama <i><a href="/wiki/That%27s_Life_(2000_TV_series)" title="That's Life (2000 TV series)">That's Life</a></i>. In January 2006, she starred as an <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_Church_(United_States)" title="Episcopal Church (United States)">Episcopal</a> bishop in the NBC comedy-drama series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Book_of_Daniel_(TV_series)" title="The Book of Daniel (TV series)">The Book of Daniel</a></i>. The series, which also starred <a href="/wiki/Aidan_Quinn" title="Aidan Quinn">Aidan Quinn</a> as a drug-addicted Episcopal priest married to an alcoholic wife, was met with controversy from religious and spiritual leaders due to its unconventional portrayals of religious figures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yonke_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-yonke-19">[19]</a></sup> Conservative groups including <a href="/wiki/American_Family_Association" title="American Family Association">American Family Association</a> and <a href="/wiki/Focus_on_the_Family" title="Focus on the Family">Focus on the Family</a> urged supporters to complain to NBC affiliates that carried the show. NBC pulled the series from its lineup after four episodes but did not publicly give a reason for doing so.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-camacho_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-camacho-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2006, Burstyn appeared in the drama-romance film <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Fountain_(film)" title="The Fountain (film)">The Fountain</a></i>, directed by <a href="/wiki/Darren_Aronofsky" title="Darren Aronofsky">Darren Aronofsky</a>, with whom she worked in <i>Requiem for a Dream</i>. Since 2007, she has had an occasional recurring role on the <a href="/wiki/HBO" title="HBO">HBO</a> television drama series <i><a href="/wiki/Big_Love" title="Big Love">Big Love</a></i>, playing the mother of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polygamist" title="Polygamist">polygamist</a> wife Barbara Henrickson.</p>
<p>She provided a supporting role as the mother of two sons in the drama-romance film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Elephant_King" title="The Elephant King">The Elephant King</a></i>. The film originally premiered at the <a href="/wiki/Tribeca_Film_Festival#2006_Tribeca_Film_Festival" title="Tribeca Film Festival">2006 Tribeca Film Festival</a> but did not open in U.S. theaters until October 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-goldstein_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-goldstein-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>Burstyn starred in the Broadway production of Martin Tahse's <i>Oldest Living Confederate Widow Tells All</i>, based upon <a href="/wiki/Oldest_Living_Confederate_Widow_Tells_All" title="Oldest Living Confederate Widow Tells All">the novel of the same title</a> by <a href="/wiki/Allan_Gurganus" title="Allan Gurganus">Allan Gurganus</a>. The show played 19 previews and officially opened November 17, 2003. Because of unfavorable reviews, all performances after the opening night were cancelled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-one_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-one-22">[22]</a></sup> Burstyn returned to the stage in March 2008, in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Off_Broadway" title="Off Broadway">Off-Broadway</a> production of <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Adly_Guirgis" title="Stephen Adly Guirgis">Stephen Adly Guirgis</a>'s <i>The Little Flower of East Orange</i>, directed by <a href="/wiki/Philip_Seymour_Hoffman" title="Philip Seymour Hoffman">Philip Seymour Hoffman</a> in a co-production by <a href="/wiki/LAByrinth_Theater_Company" title="LAByrinth Theater Company">LAByrinth Theater Company</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Public_Theater" title="The Public Theater">The Public Theater</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hernandez_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-hernandez-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>In addition to her stage work, Burstyn portrayed former <a href="/wiki/First_Lady_of_the_United_States" title="First Lady of the United States">First Lady</a> <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Bush" title="Barbara Bush">Barbara Bush</a> in director <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Stone" title="Oliver Stone">Oliver Stone</a>'s biographical film <i><a href="/wiki/W._(film)" title="W. (film)">W</a></i> in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-walker-mitchell_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-walker-mitchell-24">[24]</a></sup> In 2009, she won a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Awards" title="Primetime Emmy Awards">Primetime Emmy Award</a> for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Guest_Actress_%E2%80%93_Drama_Series" title="Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Guest Actress – Drama Series">Outstanding Guest Actress in a Drama Series</a> for her portrayal of the <a href="/wiki/Bipolar_disorder" title="Bipolar disorder">bipolar</a> estranged mother of Detective <a href="/wiki/Elliot_Stabler" title="Elliot Stabler">Elliot Stabler</a> on NBC's <a href="/wiki/Police_procedural" title="Police procedural">police procedural</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Law_%26_Order:_Special_Victims_Unit" title="Law &amp; Order: Special Victims Unit">Law &amp; Order: Special Victims Unit</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2014, Burstyn appeared in <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Nolan" title="Christopher Nolan">Christopher Nolan</a>'s sci-fi epic <a href="/wiki/Interstellar_(film)" title="Interstellar (film)"><i>Interstellar</i></a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sneider_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-sneider-26">[26]</a></sup> She had played <a href="/wiki/Mackenzie_Foy" title="Mackenzie Foy">Mackenzie Foy</a>'s character's grandmother in <i><a href="/wiki/Wish_You_Well_(film)" title="Wish You Well (film)">Wish You Well</a></i> the previous year, and both actresses portrayed "Murph" Cooper, albeit at radically different ages, in <i>Interstellar</i>.</p>
<p>Burstyn played Flemming, the daughter of <a href="/wiki/Blake_Lively" title="Blake Lively">Blake Lively</a>'s immortal character, in the film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Age_of_Adaline" title="The Age of Adaline">The Age of Adaline</a></i>. Production started in March 2014, and the film was released in April 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2014, Burstyn announced to direct her first feature film, <i>Bathing Flo</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ellen Burstyn is currently in development with Peter Livolsi's film "The House of Tomorrow" about her friend R. Buckminster Fuller, in which she stars and is a producer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Emmy_Awards_and_controversy">Emmy Awards and controversy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ellen_Burstyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Emmy Awards and controversy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Burstyn was nominated for an Emmy Award for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Lead_Actress_%E2%80%93_Miniseries_or_a_Movie" title="Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Lead Actress – Miniseries or a Movie">Outstanding Actress in a Miniseries or Movie</a>, for her role as <a href="/wiki/Jean_Harris" title="Jean Harris">Jean Harris</a> in the biographical <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Television_movie" title="Television movie">television film</a> <i>The People vs. Jean Harris</i> (1981) and again for another television drama film, <i>Pack of Lies</i> (1987), an adaptation of the <a href="/wiki/Pack_of_Lies" title="Pack of Lies">1983 play</a>.</p>
<p>In 2006, she was nominated for an Emmy Award for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Supporting_Actress_%E2%80%93_Miniseries_or_a_Movie" title="Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Supporting Actress – Miniseries or a Movie">Outstanding Supporting Actress in a Miniseries or Movie</a> for a role credited as "Former Tarnower Steady" in HBO's biographical television film <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mrs._Harris_(film)" title="Mrs. Harris (film)">Mrs. Harris</a></i>. (She had played <a href="/wiki/Jean_Harris" title="Jean Harris">Jean Harris</a> in <i>The People vs. Jean Harris</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-emmys_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-emmys-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>Soon after the nominations were announced, an outcry ensued from the press and the public regarding the worthiness of the nomination due to her minor role in the film, consisting of 14 seconds of screen time and 38 words of dialogue. One explanation for the nomination was that people were honoring Burstyn for her nominated but non-winning performance in the first <i>Harris</i> television film. A more popular accusation was that the nominating committee was either confused in its recollection, or merely "threw in" her name from sheer recognition, assuming a worthy performance without actually seeing it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bianco_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-bianco-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Television_Arts_%26_Sciences" title="Academy of Television Arts &amp; Sciences">Academy of Television Arts &amp; Sciences</a>, administrator of the Primetime Emmy Awards, initially insisted that "based on the popular vote, this is a legitimate nomination". Meanwhile, HBO deflected the blame for submitting the nomination to the movie-production company. Burstyn's own reaction ranged from initial silence to comments such as, "I thought it was fabulous. My next ambition is to get nominated for seven seconds, and ultimately I want to be nominated for a picture in which I don't even appear," and "This doesn't have anything to do with me. I don't even want to know about this. You people work it out yourself."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-emmynod_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-emmynod-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ultimately, <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Macdonald" title="Kelly Macdonald">Kelly Macdonald</a>, who starred in <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Girl_in_the_Cafe" title="The Girl in the Cafe">The Girl in the Cafe</a></i>, won the award.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scots_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-scots-34">[34]</a></sup> In March 2007, the Academy officially announced that eligibility for a Primetime Emmy Award in any long-form supporting-actor category required nominees to appear on-screen in at least five percent of the project.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-post_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-post-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Many critics still cite this incident to criticize the Emmy Award nomination process, claiming that name recognition has played an increasingly visible role over the years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-post_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-post-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2013, she won the Emmy Award for Outstanding Supporting Actress in a Miniseries or a Movie for <i><a href="/wiki/Political_Animals_(miniseries)" title="Political Animals (miniseries)">Political Animals</a></i>, and referenced the controversy in her acceptance speech.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_activities">Other activities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ellen_Burstyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Other activities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>During the 1970s, Burstyn was active in the movement to free convicted boxer <a href="/wiki/Rubin_Carter" title="Rubin Carter">Rubin "Hurricane" Carter</a> from jail.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-carter_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-carter-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1981, Burstyn recorded "The Ballad of the Nazi Soldier's Wife" (<a href="/wiki/Kurt_Weill" title="Kurt Weill">Kurt Weill</a>'s musical setting of <a href="/wiki/Bertolt_Brecht" title="Bertolt Brecht">Bertolt Brecht</a>'s text "<i>Und was bekam des Soldaten Weib?</i>") ('And what did the soldier's woman get?') for <a href="/wiki/Ben_Bagley" title="Ben Bagley">Ben Bagley</a>'s album <i>Kurt Weill Revisited, Vol. 2</i>.</p>
<p>Burstyn served as president of the <a href="/wiki/Actors%27_Equity_Association" title="Actors' Equity Association">Actors' Equity Association</a> from 1982 to 1985.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-equity_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-equity-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1997, Burstyn was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Women%27s_Hall_of_Fame" title="Michigan Women's Hall of Fame">Michigan Women's Hall of Fame</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MIwomens_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-MIwomens-38">[38]</a></sup> In 2000, she was named co-president of the <a href="/wiki/Actors_Studio" title="Actors Studio">Actors Studio</a>, alongside <a href="/wiki/Al_Pacino" title="Al Pacino">Al Pacino</a> and <a href="/wiki/Harvey_Keitel" title="Harvey Keitel">Harvey Keitel</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-actors_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-actors-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>She is a longtime supporter of the Democratic Party and in the documentary <i><a href="/wiki/PoliWood" title="PoliWood">PoliWood</a></i>, attends several political events of the 2008 election campaign as a supporter of <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>, commenting sadly at one point how civil competition between Democrats and Republicans no longer exists.</p>
<p>Burstyn is on the Board of Selectors of <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_Awards_for_Public_Service" title="Jefferson Awards for Public Service">Jefferson Awards for Public Service</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jefferson_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-jefferson-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ellen_Burstyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marriages_and_children">Marriages and children</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ellen_Burstyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Marriages and children">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1950, she married Bill Alexander, but they divorced in 1957. The following year, she married Paul Roberts, with whom she <a href="/wiki/Adoption" title="Adoption">adopted</a> a son named Jefferson in 1961; the couple divorced that same year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-timeline_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-timeline-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1964, she married fellow actor <a href="/wiki/Neil_Nephew" title="Neil Nephew">Neil Nephew</a>, who later changed his name to Neil Burstyn, but the union was turbulent. Neil Burstyn was <a href="/wiki/Schizophrenia" title="Schizophrenia">schizophrenic</a>; he would have episodes of violence, and eventually left her. He attempted to reconcile, but she rejected this, ultimately divorcing him in 1972. In her autobiography, <i>Lessons in Becoming Myself</i>, Burstyn revealed that he <a href="/wiki/Stalking" title="Stalking">stalked</a> her for a period of six years after their divorce. He eventually broke into her house and raped her, but no charges were filed, as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spousal_rape" title="Spousal rape">spousal rape</a> was not yet legally a crime. He died by suicide in 1978.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ellen_Burstyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Burstyn was raised <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic</a> but now affiliates herself with all religious faiths. Her spiritual journey began with <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Sufism" title="Sufism">Sufism</a>. She explains: "I am a spirit opening to the truth that lives in all of these religions... I always pray to Spirit, but sometimes it's to the Goddess. Sometimes it's to <a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">Jesus</a>... Sometimes I pray to <a href="/wiki/Ganesha" title="Ganesha">Ganesha</a> if I need an obstacle removed. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guan_Yin" title="Guan Yin">Guan Yin</a> is one of my favorite manifestations of the divine, the embodiment of compassion... So I have Guan Yin with me all the time."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reiss_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-reiss-43">[43]</a></sup> Burstyn has stated that in her late 30s she began to delve into the spiritual realm, coming under the tutelage of Sufi teacher Pir <a href="/wiki/Vilayat_Inayat_Khan" title="Vilayat Inayat Khan">Vilayat Inayat Khan</a>; he gave her the spiritual name Hadiya, which means "she who guides" in <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Filmography">Filmography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ellen_Burstyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Filmography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
